## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration (dv_dt) depends on velocity (v) and time (t), suggesting velocity-dependent nonlinear forces (damping/driving) and possibly position encoded implicitly through time-dependent terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear velocity-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (linear drag force)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type oscillator nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping/driving)
- Restoring force via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) (position implicitly as sinusoidal function of time)
- Nonlinear restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (damped oscillator with implicit position)
- Duffing-type via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 (cubic restoring force with implicit x ~ sin(ωt))
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (linear damping with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol full: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (self-excited oscillator with restoring force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (quadratic velocity-dependent drag)
- Polynomial velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)
- Combined restoring and damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v (Duffing with damping)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Coulomb + viscous friction: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sign(v) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (mixed friction model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Velocity-squared terms (v**2 or v*abs(v)) → nonlinear/quadratic damping or drag forces
- Product (1 - c*v**2)*v → self-excited oscillation (Van der Pol type) with amplitude-limiting mechanism
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v**3) → symmetric nonlinear damping preserving time-reversal antisymmetry
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t), cos(c*t) → implicit position representation or external periodic driving
- Cubic sinusoidal terms sin(c*t)**3 → Duffing-type cubic restoring force with implicit harmonic position
- Mixed v and trigonometric time terms → coupled damping and restoring force dynamics
- Product of velocity and trigonometric time v*sin(c*t) → parametric coupling between velocity and position-like variable
- Sign function of velocity sign(v) → Coulomb/dry friction forces that oppose motion direction

GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidate formulas: 53

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)` = `0.9384*sin(t) - 0.8670*sin(v)`.

The GT has two terms: a sine function of `t` and a sine function of `v`. The key challenge is that most candidates use polynomial approximations of `sin(v)` (like `c0*v + c1*v**3 + c5*v**5 + ...`) combined with sinusoidal functions of `t`.

**Key insight:** The Taylor series of `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - v⁷/5040 + ...`. So `-beta*sin(v)` can be approximated by polynomial terms in `v`, but it can **never be exactly equal** to a finite polynomial in `v`. The question is whether any candidate has `sin(v)` explicitly or can achieve exact equivalence.

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` explicitly. They all use polynomials in `v` (like `v, v³, v⁵, v⁷`) or expressions like `v*exp(c*v²)`, `v*|v|`, `v/(cv²+1)`, `log(...)`, etc.

Let me check if any non-polynomial terms could equal `sin(v)`:

- **`v*exp(c*v²)`**: This is `v * Σ(c*v²)^n/n!` = `v + cv³ + c²v⁵/2 + ...`. For `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`, the signs alternate, but `exp(c*v²)` with negative `c` gives `v - |c|v³ + c²v⁵/2 - ...`. The coefficients don't match `sin(v)` (ratio test: `-1/6` vs `c`, `1/120` vs `c²/2` → `c = -1/6`, `c²/2 = 1/72 ≠ 1/120`). Not exact.

- **`log(c*exp(c*v²) + 1)`**: Not equivalent to `sin(v)`.

- **Polynomial `v + v³ + v⁵ + v⁷ + v⁹ + v¹¹`** (candidate 37): Still a finite polynomial, cannot equal `sin(v)` exactly.

- **`v/(c*v² + 1)`**: This is a rational function, not `sin(v)`.

- **Candidates with `v*|v|`** (24, 25, 38, etc.): Since `v*|v|` is not equivalent to any term in `sin(v)` (which is odd and smooth), and we're in a physics domain where `v` takes negative values, these don't help achieve exact equivalence.

- **Candidate 10**: `c0*v + c1*v³ + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t)³ + c5*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c6*v⁵ + c7*v⁷` — This has shared parameters between the sin³ and sin terms, but still only polynomials in `v`.

- **Candidate 11**: Has rational functions in `v` with `cos` terms in `t`. The `v`-dependent part is rational, not `sin(v)`.

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` as an explicit term. All candidates represent the `v`-dependence through polynomials, exponentials, absolute values, rational functions, or logarithms — none of which can be **exactly** equivalent to `sin(v)` for all values of `v`.

The question asks about **mathematical equivalence**, not approximation. Since `sin(v)` is a transcendental function that cannot be represented exactly by any finite polynomial, rational function, exponential, or combination thereof (other than its own definition via complex exponentials, which aren't available here), none of these candidates can be made exactly equivalent to the GT.

No candidate can achieve exact mathematical equivalence to `F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)`.
